**GT: 7.317*epsilon³ + 7.950*(T - 287.09)*exp(-epsilon)**

The GT has three basis functions: **epsilon³**, **T*exp(-epsilon)**, and **exp(-epsilon)**.

Let me analyze each candidate systematically.

### Candidate 1:
`T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + c2*exp(c3/(c4+epsilon)) + c5 + c6*exp(T*c7*epsilon) + c8*epsilon*exp(T*c9)`

### Candidate 2:

### Candidate 3:

### Candidate 38:

Interesting. T*c1*exp(c2*epsilon): if c2=-1, this gives T*c1*exp(-epsilon) = c1*T*exp(-epsilon). That matches the T*exp(-epsilon) term!

c3*exp(c4*epsilon): if c4=-1, gives c3*exp(-epsilon). That matches the exp(-epsilon) term!

But we still need epsilon³. T*c0*epsilon is T*epsilon. The last term: c5*exp(T*c6/(T+c7) + c8/(T+c9)). 

For this to contribute epsilon³, it would need to be a polynomial in epsilon, which exp can't provide unless the argument is 0 (making it constant). If c6=0 and c8=0, this is just c5 (constant). So we'd have:

T*c0*epsilon + c1*T*exp(-epsilon) + c3*exp(-epsilon) + c5

This gives us T*epsilon, T*exp(-epsilon), exp(-epsilon), and constant. But we need epsilon³, not T*epsilon. We can set c0=0 to eliminate T*epsilon, but then we have no epsilon³ term.

No way to get epsilon³.
**Candidate 38 verdict: [NO MATCH]**
